  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aeab1889-d585-41e5-924a-ca32fede6c53'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

Desperate to break the intimacy of their telepathic link, he becomes the enemy and hunter of Kaitlyn's group. Rob is determined to destroy Gabriel if he has to ... but Kait can't let that happen. On her own, she leaves her friends and returns to the Institute, pretending to join Mr. Zetes. But when her reckless gamble goes wrong, will Gabriel save her—or betray her again? And when the final battle comes, will Kaitlyn choose Rob or Gabriel—light or darkness?</span>

<div id="review_354819739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354819739" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354819739?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354819739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13980410255652009641">The Passion is such a fitting name for this last novel in L.J. Smith's Dark Visions Trilogy. In this installment, Kaitlyn is forced to travel to the Institute, take advantage of Gabriel's feelings for her, and destroy Mr. Z's evil plans. Having convinced Gabriel, Joyce, and most of the warped up members of the Institute of her loyalty, Kaitlyn must somehow plan to destroy the crystal and keep the shard of the Fellowship's pure crystal from falling into Mr. Z's power. However, little does Kaitlyn</span>
  <span id="freeText13980410255652009641" style="display:none">The Passion is such a fitting name for this last novel in L.J. Smith's Dark Visions Trilogy. In this installment, Kaitlyn is forced to travel to the Institute, take advantage of Gabriel's feelings for her, and destroy Mr. Z's evil plans. Having convinced Gabriel, Joyce, and most of the warped up members of the Institute of her loyalty, Kaitlyn must somehow plan to destroy the crystal and keep the shard of the Fellowship's pure crystal from falling into Mr. Z's power. However, little does Kaitlyn realize that it isn't just Gabriel's feelings she's playing with, it could be her own as well...<br /><br />I absolutely loved this stunning conclusion to this brilliant trilogy. Although I definitely enjoyed The Forbidden Game more than this trilogy and appreciate the horror, despair, and creepiness of that series, I also found myself enjoying the wit, snarkiness, and complex relationships within this trilogy. Dark Visions is a lighter mix of paranormal, with more emphasis given on the blooming romances between Gabriel and Kaitlyn (I can hardly call what Kaitlyn and Rob had a romance) and the budding friendships between these five unlikely psychics. The Passion really puts this all to the test, strengthening the bonds between these friends and making them realize what they have.<br /><br />Yet, what I loved the most about this installment was the romance. I have been a loyal Team Gabriel shipper since the first novel and although I hated that Kaitlyn was taking advantage of his feelings, I was thrilled seeing her changes in character as well. Furthermore, I think the relationship Kaitlyn formed with the other members of the Institute this time around were not only important, but they were also imperative to her growth and their development as characters as well. In addition, although we didn't see Rob, Anna, and Lewis as much in this installment, I think the changes that Rob and Anna went through were also remarkable and I was glad to see so much character development in this one. As with the previous two novels however, Gabriel steals the show in terms of personality growth. I loved his complex personality and only wished we could see even more of him.<br /><br />Nevertheless, although I enjoyed this conclusion, I have to admit that I was expecting a little more of an earth-shattering finale. I felt as if the manner in which this situation was solved was a little too easy and I only wish it could have been dragged on a little longer to add an element of suspense to it. Yet, as far as last-books-of-a-trilogy go, this was a pretty darn good one. Thus, I would heartily recommend this series to fans of L.J. Smith, but I'd recommend starting with The Forbidden Game first. It may increase your expectations of this series to unnatural highs, but it'll definitely force you to keep reading to find the excellent writing quality that Smith's novels possess.<br /><br />You can see this review and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/06/review-passion-by-lj-smith.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13980410255652009641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332252146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16995317582024614611"><u>
  <b>Review for full series</b>
</u><br/><br/>Dark Visions is my second experience with LJ Smith. I started with The Vampire Diaries series, which was a somewhat of a letdown for me as a big fan of the show. I was iffy on starting another LJS book, but I'm glad I did. Dark Visions turned out to be just pure fun!<br/><br/>This is by no means a perfect series. <b>Compared to nowadays YA books, I have to say that Dark Visions could come off as somewhat unoriginal.</b> I mean, you've heard it before- loner girl with dead parent and mag</span>
  <span id="freeText16995317582024614611" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Review for full series</b>
</u><br /><br />Dark Visions is my second experience with LJ Smith. I started with The Vampire Diaries series, which was a somewhat of a letdown for me as a big fan of the show. I was iffy on starting another LJS book, but I'm glad I did. Dark Visions turned out to be just pure fun!<br /><br />This is by no means a perfect series. <b>Compared to nowadays YA books, I have to say that Dark Visions could come off as somewhat unoriginal.</b> I mean, you've heard it before- loner girl with dead parent and magical powers teams up with other magical teens and finds herself torn between the super nice guy and the bad boy with a good heart.<br /><br /><b>Although it did seem slightly formulaic and predictable at times, it was just a good time.</b> It's an easy read that will have you flying through the pages, eager to find out what will happen next. I loved when we would get glimpses into other characters besides Kaitlyn's POV- especially Gabriel's, his made me smile.<br /><br />I did at times feel like some of the characters were underdeveloped and didn't change much throughout the story, or at least the first book. Gabriel seemed to be the only one character that underwent any time of change, but him doing so was part of the reason I enjoyed this series.<br /><br />The last book did drag for me a bit. Gabriel is an extremely entertaining character, but by the third book there were a few times that he came off as whiny, but the end climax wrapped up the story very nicely.<br /><br /><b>A great read if you're not going to look into it too much.</b> It's just pure entertainment and I do think that I will be picking more of LJ's books up at some point because of this.<br /><br /><br /><b>Random thought:</b> Was anyone else kind of creeped out by Rob? That whole 'he doesn't understand girls' thing made no sense to me whatsoever and just took his character to a creepy level.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16995317582024614611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13700266686145705941" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 5/5<br /><p><br /><b>Cover:</b> 3/5 - Not a huge fan of the photography or artwork <br /><br /></p><p><br /><u>The Passion</u> is the last book in the <i>Dark Visions</i> trilogy by L.J Smith. At first I though tit would be another vampire novel but it isn't. This is great for any teen to read who really likes fantasy. The book shows some evil, but it just briefly touches it. The book has some tense moments in it. I couldn't put this book down. I found this to be very exciting. LJ Smith has gotten me to read everything she has written. I didn't find a moment of dullness.</span>

<div id="review_761528496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761528496" />
    <a title="Becky Courage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2597296-becky-courage"><img alt="Becky Courage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551803763p2/2597296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761528496?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky Courage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky Courage" href="/user/show/2597296-becky-courage">Becky Courage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761528496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17163037530514062515">The Passion by LJ Smith is the third and final book in the Dark Visions Trilogy. <br/>Here is a spoiler play by play of what happened in this novel:<br/><br/>The novel starts off with Gabriel having changed sides. He is now on a quest to be evil and powerful, and is hunting Kait, Rob, Anna and Lewis (the gang) to get the crystal. In his mind, he is pure evil. He’s against them all and shows no mercy. He is working for Mr. Zete’s and is back at the institute. Lydia also ran away with him to be back under the co</span>
  <span id="freeText17163037530514062515" style="display:none">The Passion by LJ Smith is the third and final book in the Dark Visions Trilogy. <br />Here is a spoiler play by play of what happened in this novel:<br /><br />The novel starts off with Gabriel having changed sides. He is now on a quest to be evil and powerful, and is hunting Kait, Rob, Anna and Lewis (the gang) to get the crystal. In his mind, he is pure evil. He’s against them all and shows no mercy. He is working for Mr. Zete’s and is back at the institute. Lydia also ran away with him to be back under the control of her father. The gang (Anna, Rob and Lewis) want to hurt Gabriel because he betrayed them, but Kait doesn’t want to see him harmed. In the middle of the night she runs away to the Institute with a plan. She ends up getting attacked before she reaches the institute, but Gabriel saves her. (Of course he’s going to save the woman he loves! Forget the crystal and having to hunt her.) <br />	<br />She’s got a plan to convince everyone that she’s turned evil too, in order to gain access to the institute, its information, and the whereabouts of the crystal so she can destroy it and take down Mr. Zete’s. She’s really a spy trying to destroy the crystal and Mr. Zete’s’ evil. Gabriel believes her lies and they connect again- through energy and through lips! <br />	<br />Mr. Zete’s and Joyce decide to let her stay- although there is suspicion about her true intentions. She meets the other students- the mental ones from the pilot study who were the grey people that attacked the gang back in Book 2. They're pretty wild and she learns that the routines of the institute have changed a lot. She’s looking for the crystal and information on how to destroy it. She’s having trouble tricking the others into believing she’s on their side. Gabriel is very suspicious when she won’t open her mind to him.<br />	<br />Rob, Anna and Lewis figure Kait went to the institute, and they meet up with her at school to get things cleared up. She tells them her plan of being a spy, and they decide to let her stay at the institute, and they also want to help her. Throughout the novel Kait has been having an internal struggle over her feelings towards Gabriel. She knows he loves her- but does she love him? The gang has the crystal and use it to help Marisol- a woman who worked at the institute, who didn’t trust Joyce or Mr. Zete’s and who warned them early on to leave. Rob and Anna start this weird emotional bond thing. I feel like it was pieced into the writing for the sake of filling later on story plots. Possibly allowing for Kait and Gabriel to be together?<br />	<br />Gabriel senses that Kait is lying to him and the Institute when he feels the rest of the group in the web being nearby. Gabriel and Kait get into a fight. Then Joyce tells them of a job- breaking into a law firm? (I thought this was weird). They continue to conduct tests geared towards crime. I assume Zete’s is training their powers for crimes. Gabriel is not speaking to Kait- he knows that she is a spy and didn’t really turn to the evil side. Lydia suspects also. <br /><br />Joyce tested Kait and put a piece of crystal on her head which caused her personality to be different. Uh oh- she’s losing her mind. The psychic teens killed some of the ancestors using their psychic powers and the influence of the crystal. Now the gang doesn’t have any help. <br /><br />Kait is still investigating. She needs to find out the combination lock to a secret room where she thinks the crystal is being kept. She’s also in contact with Rob, trying to get the pure shard. She's becoming super sacrificial and annoying. At a party she figures out how to break the combination code. She breaks into the crystal room but there are ‘people’ guarding it. <br /><br />The psychic teens, Joyce and Mr. Zete’s come to the room, figure out she is a spy and capture her. Dun dun dun! They are going to punish Kait for being a traitor. Lydia, Joyce and some of the other psychic teens actually stand up for her, but Mr. Zete’s has complete control and power over them. <br />They place her in underwater isolation tank, cutting off all senses. She has out of body experiences and begins to lose herself. Gabriel is freaking out- because he really does love Kait. He connects with her mind and sends her images and sensations to keep her sane. They admit they love each other. Aww. Rob has had enough of standing by, and he and the gang are coming to the institute to save Kait. <br /><br />Zete’s is going to try to kill Kait with the giant crystal. Just as they pile into the crystal room, boom the gang breaks in! Joyce, Lydia and some others turn against Z and refuse to kill Kait and the gang. Gabriel gets a hold of the pure shard and is going to destroy the crystal. A struggle occurs but of course good prevails and the crystal is destroyed, taking Mr. Zete’s along with it. <br /><br />Everyone is happy, much hugging ensues. Joyce was under some spell which she has now snapped out of. Everyone makes up and reconnects. Gabriel and Kait end up together. (Duh!) They have Rob’s blessing. Anna and Rob get together (my prediction was right!) and so do Lewis and Lydia. <br /><br />I think Gabriel was cured of his psychic vampire curse- it wasn’t super clear in the ending. They’re all still connected in the web, but for some reason it doesn’t matter any more and they are just going to live with it. That got swept under the rug pretty quickly. <br /><br />In the end, everyone is happy, good has overcome evil and they are going back to Canada to live with the remaining fellowship. The end. <br /><br />Thoughts:<br /><br />I give this book a three as I did with the other two. Overall, the entire series gets a 3 stars. <br />I really enjoyed the mystery and suspense. The love story was not my favourite- however Gabriel and Kait made more sense than Rob and Kait because they actually have a connection. <br />I ended up not minding all of the crystal hooplaw- it was interesting. Overall, the book was nothing profound and amazing, pretty typical LJ Smith, but it was entertaining. Im glad it was a switch up from vampires. <br /><br />If you're in the mood for a fast paced series with suspense and uber cheesy and predictable characters, pick this up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17163037530514062515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7586035981762330601">After their time at the White House, Kaitlyn, Anna, Lewis & Rob seek refuge at Marisol’s house. But not Gabriel. Oh no! He is now working for Mr. Z. The only thing he wants from his former friends is the last remaining shard & then he can go back to the Institute.   <span id="freeText7586035981762330601" style="display:none">After their time at the White House, Kaitlyn, Anna, Lewis &amp; Rob seek refuge at Marisol’s house. But not Gabriel. Oh no! He is now working for Mr. Z. The only thing he wants from his former friends is the last remaining shard &amp; then he can go back to the Institute. Kaitlyn decides to follow him but is shocked by the many changes she sees at the Institute. 1) Its absolutely filthy 2) Joyce is still working there 3) There is new students &amp; 4) The experiments they do are very dark &amp; dangerous. Kaitlyn wants to take down Mr. Z once &amp; for all. But with her friends many of miles away &amp; Gabriel not talking to her, would she actually be able to do it? Can she stop Mr. Z &amp; take down the Institute?<br /><br />I thought this series was good &amp; this is simply down to Gabriel. He is moody, dark &amp; cynical &amp; yet he is willing to do anything to protect Kaitlyn which is so sweet. The only thing I didn’t like was this whole Anna &amp; Rob thing which came out of nowhere. But other than that, it is a good series. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <span id="freeText12448147862588193008" style="display:none">Overall this trilogy works better than Night World because we had 3 books for the same group of characters and that gave everything at least some time to develop, but the story still remains super simplistic and faced paced with rapid fire plot points and developments. <br /><br />I liked it more as a teenager, so I suppose for a 14-15 year old these would probably be entertaining on a more worthwhile level, but for me at 24 the books are just kinda generally engaging enough for me to get through them. //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HJ4GaSi/DDDz8colF8UZSpX4+XvyKZNDLht7Wi3TafAtNo5U1k7KyDppsUfMRUqkXMiZ0BHp97OEFPLb0Waz1w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('axayRXLjL/ajBziyybn6i5QYkcjBcYG3SirZ/0bcm2havjp4jBLpDmqfQ9ASOallXSjxYyKx5UfgJVB+umlBTw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

In A Gift of Hope, she shows us how she transformed that pain into a campaign<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1314257909753855360\" style=\"display:none\">In her powerful memoir His Bright Light, #1 New York Times bestselling author Danielle Steel opened her heart to share the devastating story of the loss of her beloved son. In A Gift of Hope, she shows us how she transformed that pain into a campaign of service that enriched her life beyond what she could imagine.   For eleven years, Danielle Steel took to the streets with a small team to help the homeless of San Francisco. She worked anonymously, visiting the “cribs” of the city’s most vulnerable citizens under cover of darkness, distributing food, clothing, bedding, tools, and toiletries. She sought no publicity for her efforts and remained anonymous throughout. Now she is speaking to bring attention to their plight.   In this unflinchingly honest and deeply moving memoir, the famously private author speaks out publicly for the first time about her work among the most desperate members of our society. She offers achingly acute portraits of the people she met along the way—and issues a heartfelt call for more effective action to aid this vast, deprived population. Determined to supply the homeless with the basic necessities to keep them alive, she ends up giving them something far more powerful: a voice.   By turns candid and inspirational, Danielle Steel’s A Gift of Hope is a true act of advocacy and love.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1314257909753855360\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6240511892294780422">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series'>https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br/><br/><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in th</span>
  <span id="freeText6240511892294780422" style="display:none">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series">https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br /><br /><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in the Bay Area of California, with a backyard that is full of flowers, which she adores, especially with many different shades of roses.<br /><br />She loves to visit a friend's little cabin in the Point Reyes National Seashore area, which has lots of trees, lots of animals, lots of beaches to walk on, and lots of places to hike. Once, while hiking, she saw a snow-white buck which allowed her to follow it nearly half a mile. She also likes to collect things: angels (they remind her of her late mother), tiny boxes from different countries or of fanciful shape, nineteenth century children's literature, and books about quantum physics--especially about the mystery of the dark energy in the universe. A militant optimist, she is also part of the Velociraptor Sisterhood (a fancy way of saying that she likes to read, write and discuss books with strong female characters), and she has traveled extensively in Europe and the Far East. The two countries she loves to visit most are Great Britain, with its historic monuments and amazing country landscapes, and Japan, with its bustling urban life and exquisite mountain scenery.<br /><br />Her favorite current writer is Terry Pratchett, the author of the Discworld series, for its wild and witty satires on life, death, war, love, assassins, coppers, and Australia. Her favorite classical writer is Jane Austen. Her favorite poets are Robert Frost and Emily Dickinson. Her favorite movies are The Seven Samurai and Avatar (analyze that!). She doesn't have a favorite TV show, because she doesn't have time to watch TV (and only owns one for playing movies).<br /><br />Her favorite people are her readers, each of whom she cherishes with deep and lasting affection.<br /><br /><i>Note: L. J. Smith wrote books 1-7 of The Vampire Diaries series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. wrote books 1-3 of The Secret Circle series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. did not write any of the Originals or Stefan's Diaries. These were written by Kevin Williamson and/or various ghostwritters.</i> <br /></span>
